10.1016/j.jmp.2022.102743
Knowledge structure theory was established by  Doignon and Falmagne (1985) , which conceives items as being dichotomous. It categorizes the responses into the dichotomy of “mastering” vs. “not mastering” an item (or, “solving” vs. “not solving”, respectively). Recently,  Stefanutti et al. (2020)  and  Heller (2021)  extended the binary case to a (complete) lattice  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       where  
                         L 
                       is the set of response values and  
                         ≤ 
                       is a partial order on  
                         L 
                      , which can be identified with different types, or degrees of mastering. Moreover, they provided some characterizations of the resulting polytomous knowledge structures that are based on the domain  
                         Q 
                       consisting of items and the (complete) lattice  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       consisting of response values. Such findings open the field to a systematic generalization of knowledge structure theory to the polytomous case.

In knowledge structure theory, a number of one-to-one correspondences were established between particular collections of mathematical structures. Specially,  Doignon and Falmagne (1999)  extended the one-to-one correspondence between quasi ordinal spaces and quasi orders obtained by  Birkhoff (1937)  and established a one-to-one correspondence between granular knowledge spaces on the domain  
                         Q 
                       and surmise functions on  
                         Q 
                       (also see Theorem 5.2.5 in  Falmagne & Doignon, 2011 ). Recently, as an adaptation to the polytomous framework of the Doignon–Falmagne’s result,  Stefanutti et al. (2020)  gave the following theorem.

Theorem 11 in 
                      Stefanutti et al. (2020) .  For the set  
                      
                         Q 
                       
                      of items and the complete lattice  
                      
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       
                      of response values, let  
                      
                         
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       
                      and  
                      
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       
                      denote the collection of all granular polytomous spaces on  
                      
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            L 
                            ) 
                         
                       
                      and the collection of all polytomous surmise functions on  
                      
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            L 
                            ) 
                         
                      
                      , respectively. Then there is a one-to-one correspondence between  
                      
                         
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       
                      and  
                      
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                      
                      . It is defined, for  
                      
                         
                            K 
                            ∈ 
                            
                               
                                  K 
                               
                               
                                  ⊔ 
                               
                            
                         
                       
                      and  
                      
                         
                            μ 
                            ∈ 
                            
                               
                                  M 
                               
                               
                                  ⊔ 
                               
                            
                         
                       
                      by the formula:  
                      
                         
                            
                               C 
                             
                            is an atom at  
                            
                               q 
                             
                            in  
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               ⟺ 
                            
                            
                               C 
                             
                            is a clause for  
                            
                               q 
                             
                            in  
                            
                               μ 
                            , 
                       
                      where  
                      
                         
                            C 
                            : 
                            Q 
                            ⟶ 
                            L 
                         
                       
                      and  
                      
                         
                            q 
                            ∈ 
                            Q 
                         
                      .

Unfortunately, the above theorem does not hold true. In fact, there exists a counterexample to show that there is not any one-to-one correspondence between the collection of all granular polytomous spaces on  
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            L 
                            ) 
                         
                       and the collection of all polytomous surmise functions on  
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            L 
                            ) 
                         
                       for some set  
                         Q 
                       of items and some complete lattice  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       of response values. Here, the counterexample stems from the fact that the function  
                         
                            m 
                            : 
                            
                               
                                  K 
                               
                               
                                  ⊔ 
                               
                            
                            ⟶ 
                            
                               
                                  M 
                               
                               
                                  ⊔ 
                               
                            
                         
                       described in the proof of the above theorem need not be surjective. As an interesting work, our discussion spreads from polytomous surmise functions. It should be noticed that these discussions do not affect the rest of  Stefanutti et al. (2020) .

In this paper, we modify the concept of polytomous surmise functions to introduce polytomous surmising functions that are stronger than polytomous surmise functions. Moreover, an example is given to show that a polytomous surmise function need not be a polytomous surmising function. Let  
                         Q 
                       be a set of items and  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       a complete lattice of response values. We prove that there exists a one-to-one correspondence  
                         f 
                       between the collection of all granular polytomous spaces on  
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            L 
                            ) 
                         
                       and the collection of all polytomous surmising functions on  
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            L 
                            ) 
                         
                      , where polytomous surmising functions cannot be replaced with polytomous surmise functions. This result gives a correction of Theorem 11 in  Stefanutti et al. (2020) . In addition, as an application of the correspondence  
                         f 
                      , we show that the pair  
                         
                            ( 
                            f 
                            , 
                            
                               
                                  f 
                               
                               
                                  − 
                                  1 
                               
                            
                            ) 
                         
                       of mappings forms a Galois connection where all granular polytomous spaces and all polytomous surmising functions are closed elements of this Galois connection.

In this section, we give some preliminaries including definitions and known results of the polytomous theory of knowledge structures, which will be useful in our discussion.

Recall that a binary relation  
                         R 
                       on a set  
                         B 
                       is a quasi order if  
                         R 
                       is reflexive and transitive; a quasi order  
                         R 
                       on  
                         B 
                       is a partial order if  
                         R 
                       is antisymmetric. Given the set  
                         L 
                       of response values and a partial order  
                         ≤ 
                       on  
                         L 
                      , the relational structure  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       is called a response scale. The basic assumption in what follows is that  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       is a lattice. This means that for all pairs of elements in  
                         L 
                       there exist a supremum (least upper bound w.r.t.  
                         ≤ 
                      ) and an infimum (greatest lower bound w.r.t.  
                         ≤ 
                      ). Using an algebraic notation, suprema and infima are denoted by the binary operations join  
                         ∨ 
                       and meet  
                         ∧ 
                      , i.e.,  
                         
                            v 
                            ∨ 
                            w 
                            = 
                            sup 
                            
                               { 
                               v 
                               , 
                               w 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            v 
                            ∧ 
                            w 
                            = 
                            inf 
                            
                               { 
                               v 
                               , 
                               w 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       for all  
                         
                            v 
                            , 
                            w 
                            ∈ 
                            L 
                         
                      . Further,  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       is a complete lattice if for every subset  
                         
                            S 
                            ⊆ 
                            L 
                         
                      ,  
                         S 
                       has both a supremum (least upper bound w.r.t.  
                         ≤ 
                      ) and an infimum (greatest lower bound w.r.t.  
                         ≤ 
                      ), where supremum of  
                         S 
                       and infimum of  
                         S 
                       are denoted by  
                         
                            sup 
                            S 
                         
                       and  
                         
                            inf 
                            S 
                         
                       respectively. In this paper, for a complete lattice  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                      ,  
                         
                            inf 
                            L 
                         
                       and  
                         
                            sup 
                            L 
                         
                       always are denoted by  
                         0 
                       and  
                         1 
                      , respectively. A single response value  
                         
                            x 
                            ∈ 
                            L 
                         
                       is said to be irreducible (see  Stefanutti et al., 2020 ) if, for all subsets  
                         
                            G 
                            ⊆ 
                            L 
                         
                      ,  
                         
                            sup 
                            G 
                            = 
                            x 
                         
                       implies  
                         
                            x 
                            ∈ 
                            G 
                         
                      . For a complete lattice  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                      ,  
                         
                            
                               L 
                            
                            
                               + 
                            
                         
                       always denotes the subset of all the irreducible response values of  
                         L 
                      . By convention, the supremum of an empty set of response values is  
                         0 
                      
 ( 
                         
                            sup 
                            0̸ 
                            = 
                            0 
                         
                      ), therefore  
                         
                            0 
                            ⁄ 
                            ∈ 
                            
                               
                                  L 
                               
                               
                                  + 
                               
                            
                         
                       (see  Stefanutti et al., 2020 ).

Let  
                         Q 
                       be a set of items and  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       a complete lattice of response values. Then each polytomous knowledge state is formally a mapping  
                         
                            K 
                            : 
                            Q 
                            → 
                            L 
                         
                      . Let  
                         
                            
                               L 
                            
                            
                               Q 
                            
                         
                       denote the collection of all possible polytomous knowledge states, i.e., the set of all mappings  
                         
                            Q 
                            → 
                            L 
                         
                      . Alternatively, a polytomous knowledge state  
                         K 
                       may be considered as a particular subset of  
                         
                            Q 
                            × 
                            L 
                         
                      . By convention, two trivial polytomous knowledge states are described as follows.

(1)  
                         
                            Φ 
                            : 
                            Q 
                            → 
                            L 
                         
                       is defined by  
                         
                            Φ 
                            
                               ( 
                               q 
                               ) 
                            
                            = 
                            0 
                         
                       for all  
                         
                            q 
                            ∈ 
                            Q 
                         
                      .

(2)  
                         
                            Ω 
                            : 
                            Q 
                            → 
                            L 
                         
                       is defined by  
                         
                            Ω 
                            
                               ( 
                               q 
                               ) 
                            
                            = 
                            1 
                         
                       for all  
                         
                            q 
                            ∈ 
                            Q 
                         
                      .

The definition of a state as a mapping from items to response values induces a natural ordering on the collection  
                         
                            
                               L 
                            
                            
                               Q 
                            
                         
                       (see  Stefanutti et al., 2020 ) : given two mappings  
                         
                            
                               
                                  K 
                               
                               
                                  1 
                               
                            
                            , 
                            
                               
                                  K 
                               
                               
                                  2 
                               
                            
                            ∈ 
                            
                               
                                  L 
                               
                               
                                  Q 
                               
                            
                         
                      ,  
                         
                            
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        1 
                                     
                                  
                                  ⊑ 
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        2 
                                     
                                  
                                  ⟺ 
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        1 
                                     
                                  
                                  
                                     ( 
                                     q 
                                     ) 
                                  
                                  ≤ 
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        2 
                                     
                                  
                                  
                                     ( 
                                     q 
                                     ) 
                                  
                                  
                                  f 
                                  o 
                                  r 
                                  
                                  a 
                                  l 
                                  l 
                                  
                                  q 
                                  ∈ 
                                  Q 
                                  .

Clearly,  
                         
                            Φ 
                            ⊑ 
                            K 
                            ⊑ 
                            Ω 
                         
                       for all  
                         
                            K 
                            ∈ 
                            
                               
                                  L 
                               
                               
                                  Q 
                               
                            
                         
                      . In addition, it is not difficult to see that  
                         ⊑ 
                       is a partial order on the set  
                         
                            
                               L 
                            
                            
                               Q 
                            
                         
                       of mappings. Indeed,  
                         
                            
                               L 
                            
                            
                               Q 
                            
                         
                       is itself a complete lattice, since infima and suprema exist for all of its subsets in virtue of the existence of infima and suprema for all subsets of  
                         L 
                       (see,  Stefanutti et al., 2020 ). Now we may give the following definition for polytomous knowledge structures in the sense of  Stefanutti et al. (2020) , which will be used throughout this paper.

Definition 1 
                         
                            Stefanutti et al., 2020 
                         
                         Let  
                               Q 
                             be a set of items and  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  L 
                                  , 
                                  ≤ 
                                  ) 
                               
                             a complete lattice of response values. A polytomous knowledge structure on the pair  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  L 
                                  ) 
                               
                             is a triple  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  L 
                                  , 
                                  K 
                                  ) 
                               
                             where  
                               K 
                             is a nonempty collection of polytomous knowledge states. For convenience, we also say that  
                               K 
                             is a polytomous knowledge structure to mean that  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  L 
                                  , 
                                  K 
                                  ) 
                               
                             is a polytomous knowledge structure.

Remark 1 
                         The polytomous knowledge structure

                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  L

                                  K 
                                  ) 
                               
                             in  Definition 1  is weaker than that of  Heller (2021) , who considers  
                               K

                               Φ

                               Ω

The polytomous knowledge structure  
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            L 
                            , 
                            K 
                            ) 
                         
                       is finite if  
                         K 
                       is finite (see,  Stefanutti et al., 2020 ). It is clear that, depending on the properties of the two sets  
                         Q 
                       and  
                         L 
                      , the  
                         K 
                       may be either finite or infinite. For example, if both  
                         Q 
                       and  
                         L 
                       are finite then  
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            L 
                            , 
                            K 
                            ) 
                         
                       is obviously finite (see,  Stefanutti et al., 2020 ). In addition, more specific structural assumptions on the collection of polytomous knowledge states have received particular attention, among them the polytomous knowledge spaces.

Then  
                               K 
                             is said to be an atom at  
                               q 
                             if it is a  
                               t

                               q

Similar to the dichotomous case,  Stefanutti et al. (2020)  showed that a polytomous knowledge structure need not to have a basis. In addition, the following result was also obtained by  Stefanutti et al. (2020) .

Proposition 1 
                         
                            Stefanutti et al., 2020 
                         
                         
                            A polytomous knowledge structure  
                            
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  L 
                                  , 
                                  K 
                                  ) 
                               
                             
                            admits at most one basis.

A polytomous knowledge structure  
                            
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  L 
                                  , 
                                  K 
                                  ) 
                               
                             
                            admits at most one basis.

In (dichotomous) knowledge structure theory, the collection of all the atoms of a knowledge structure is the basis of the structure.  Stefanutti et al. (2020)  showed that this is still valid in the polytomous framework.

Proposition 2 
                         
                            Stefanutti et al., 2020 
                         
                         
                            The basis of a polytomous knowledge structure is the collection of all of its atoms.

The basis of a polytomous knowledge structure is the collection of all of its atoms.

There is one further property of the basis that holds in the dichotomous case and may not hold in the polytomous one. In (dichotomous) knowledge structure theory, if a knowledge space possesses a basis  
                         ℬ 
                      , then it equals the so-called “span” of  
                         ℬ 
                      , which is the collection of all possible unions of subfamilies of  
                         ℬ 
                       (Definition 1.19 in  Doignon & Falmagne, 1999 ). This property of the basis may no longer hold with polytomous knowledge structures, and the nature of the set  
                         L 
                       of levels is crucial in this respect. To clarify this, the notion of “span” was extended to the polytomous knowledge structures by  Stefanutti et al. (2020) .

Definition 5 
                         
                            Stefanutti et al., 2020 
                         
                         Let  
                               Q 
                             be a set of items and  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  L 
                                  , 
                                  ≤ 
                                  )

                                  ℱ 
                                  ⊆ 
                                  
                                     
                                        L 
                                     
                                     
                                        Q 
                                     
                                  
                               
                             of mappings is the family  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        ℱ 
                                     
                                     
                                        ′

                                        L 
                                     
                                     
                                        Q 
                                     
                                  
                               
                             containing any mapping which is the supremum  
                               
                                  ⨆ 
                                  G 
                               
                             of some subfamily  
                               
                                  G 
                                  ⊆ 
                                  ℱ 
                               
                            . In such case we say that  
                               ℱ 
                             spans  
                               
                                  
                                     ℱ 
                                  
                                  
                                     ′ 
                                  
                               
                            . For the sake of convenience, we write  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        ℱ 
                                     
                                     
                                        ′ 
                                     
                                  
                                  = 
                                  S 
                                  
                                     ( 
                                     ℱ 
                                     ) 
                                  
                               
                             to denote that  
                               ℱ 
                             spans  
                               
                                  
                                     ℱ 
                                  
                                  
                                     ′ 
                                  
                               
                             here.

Stefanutti et al. (2020)  gave two examples to show, respectively, one case where the basis spans the whole structure and one case where the span of the basis is a proper subset of the whole structure. Which class of polytomous knowledge structures can be spanned by its basis? Granularity is a sufficient condition under which a polytomous knowledge space is spanned by its basis. So the notion of granularity is needed in the polytomous case too, though in a more general guise.

                                  K

                                  K

                       (see  Stefanutti et al., 2020 ).

The conditions (1) and (3) in  Definition 8 , which belong to  Stefanutti et al. (2020) , are the same as the conditions (1) and (3) in  Definition 7 . The condition (2) in  Definition 8  is a modification of the condition (2) in  Definition 7 , which is obtained by adding  
                         
                            
                               
                                  C 
                               
                               
                                  ′

                                     ′

                            C

                                     q 
                                  
                                  
                                     ′ 
                                  
                               
                               ) 
                            
                         
                       to the condition (2) in  Definition 7 . So the condition (2) in  Definition 8  is stronger than the condition (2) in  Definition 7 . Thus, any polytomous surmisal function is a polytomous surmise function. For general polytomous attribution  
                         μ 
                       on the pair  
                         
                            (

                               q

                       is irreducible for each

                            ⋃

                               0

In this section, by default if not mentioned otherwise, the letter  
                         Q 
                       always denotes a nonempty set of items and  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       a complete lattice consisting of a nonempty set  
                         L 
                       of response values with a partial order  
                         ≤ 
                       on  
                         L 
                      , where  
                         Q 
                       and  
                         L 
                       need not be finite. All polytomous knowledge structures (resp. all polytomous attributions) are on the pair  
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            L 
                            ) 
                         
                      ; polytomous knowledge structure (resp. polytomous knowledge space) is abbreviated to polytomous structure (resp. polytomous space). In addition, we also use the following notations where  
                         
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       come from  Stefanutti et al. (2020) .

                         (1)  
                               
                                  
                                     K 
                                  
                                  
                                     ⊔ 
                                  
                               
                             denotes the collection of all granular polytomous spaces on  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  L 
                                  ) 
                               
                            . 
                         (2)  
                               
                                  
                                     M 
                                  
                                  
                                     ⊔ 
                                  
                               
                             denotes the collection of all polytomous surmise functions on  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  L 
                                  ) 
                               
                            . 
                         (3)  
                               
                                  
                                     M

                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  L 
                                  ) 
                               
                            . 
                         (4)  
                               
                                  
                                     M 
                                  
                                  
                                     ∨ 
                                  
                               
                             denotes the collection of all polytomous surmising functions on  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  L 
                                  ) 
                               
                            .

The following lemma is obtained from  Definitions 7 and 8  immediately.

Lemma 1

                               . That is, the following two implications hold.

(1) Any polytomous surmising function is a polytomous surmisal function.

(2) Any polytomous surmisal function is a polytomous surmise function.

The following two examples show that no one of the implications in  Lemma 1  can be reversed.

Example 1 
                            There exists a polytomous surmise function that is not a polytomous surmisal function.

                                                 , 
                                                 1 
                                                 , 
                                                 1 
                                                 ) 
                                              
                                              } 
                                           
                                           . 
                                        
                                     
                                  
                                It is not difficult to check that  
                                  μ

                                     C 
                                     = 
                                     
                                        ( 
                                        1

                                        a

                                     C

                                        c 
                                        ) 
                                     
                                     = 
                                     1 
                                     > 
                                     0 
                                  
                               . The only  
                                  
                                     
                                        
                                           C 
                                        
                                        
                                           ′ 
                                        
                                     
                                     ∈ 
                                     μ 
                                     
                                        ( 
                                        c 
                                        )

                                        ( 
                                        c

                                     = 
                                     C

                                        c

                                        1 
                                        , 
                                        1 
                                        , 
                                        1 
                                        ) 
                                     
                                  
                               , but

                                        1

                                     ⊑

                                does not hold. This shows that  
                                  μ

                                  μ 
                                is not a polytomous surmisal function. □

Example 2 
                            There exists a polytomous surmisal function that is not a polytomous surmising function.

                                        ∪ 
                                     
                                  
                               . More precisely, we have the following. 
                            (1) If  
                                  Q 
                                and  
                                  L 
                                is described as in  Example 1 , then there is not any one-to-one correspondence between  
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⊔ 
                                     
                                  
                                and  
                                  
                                     
                                        M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⊔ 
                                     
                                  
                               . 
                            (2) If  
                                  Q 
                                and  
                                  L 
                                is described as in  Example 2 , then there is not any one-to-one correspondence between  
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⊔ 
                                     
                                  
                                and  
                                  
                                     
                                        M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∪ 
                                     
                                  
                               .

M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∨ 
                                     
                                  
                                in  Theorem 2  cannot be replaced with  
                                  
                                     
                                        M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⊔ 
                                     
                                  
                               . In fact,  
                                  
                                     
                                        M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∨ 
                                     
                                  
                                in  Theorem 2  cannot even be replaced with  
                                  
                                     
                                        M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∪ 
                                     
                                  
                               . More precisely, we have the following.

(1) If  
                                  Q 
                                and  
                                  L 
                                is described as in  Example 1 , then there is not any one-to-one correspondence between  
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⊔ 
                                     
                                  
                                and  
                                  
                                     
                                        M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⊔ 
                                     
                                  
                               .

(2) If  
                                  Q 
                                and  
                                  L 
                                is described as in  Example 2 , then there is not any one-to-one correspondence between  
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⊔ 
                                     
                                  
                                and  
                                  
                                     
                                        M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∪ 
                                     
                                  
                               .

Proof 
                            The proofs of (1) and (2) are similar, so we only prove (1). Let  
                                  Q 
                                and  
                                  L 
                                be described as in  Example 1 . If there is a one-to-one correspondence between  
                                  
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⊔ 
                                     
                                  
                                and  
                                  
                                     
                                        M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⊔ 
                                     
                                  
                               , by  Theorem 2 , then there is a one-to-one correspondence between  
                                  
                                     
                                        M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ∨ 
                                     
                                  
                                and  
                                  
                                     
                                        M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⊔ 
                                     
                                  
                               . This contradicts  Corollary 2 (1). □

The proofs of (1) and (2) are similar, so we only prove (1). Let  
                                  Q 
                                and  
                                  L 
                                be described as in  Example 1 . If there is a one-to-one correspondence between

                                        ∨ 
                                     
                                  
                                and  
                                  
                                     
                                        M 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⊔ 
                                     
                                  
                               . This contradicts  Corollary 2 (1). □

Remark 2 (1) shows that Theorem 11 in  Stefanutti et al. (2020)  does not hold true. However, we have the following result related to  Remark 2 (2), which is a direct corollary of  Theorem 2  and  Lemma 2 .

It is known that there is a one-to-one correspondence between

As an application of  Theorem 1 , we establish a Galois connection between  
                            
                               
                                  K 
                               
                               
                                  ⊔ 
                               
                            
                          and  
                            
                               
                                  M

The standard concept of a Galois connection comes from  Birkhoff (1967)  (see  Doignon & Falmagne, 1985 ), which is closely related to that of a “residuated mapping” (see e.g.  Blyth & Janowitz, 1972 ). The following definition for Galois connections slightly extends the standard concept of a Galois connection, by allowing quasi ordered sets instead of ordered sets. This construction comes from  Doignon and Falmagne (1985) . More background on Galois connections can be found in  Birkhoff (1967)  or  Barbut and Monjardet (1970) , for instance.

In this paper, we modify the concept of polytomous surmise functions to introduce polytomous surmising functions that are stronger than polytomous surmise functions. Moreover, we give an example to show that a polytomous surmise function need not be a polytomous surmising function. The further discussion spread around the correspondences between the collection of all granular polytomous spaces and the collection of all polytomous surmising functions.

Given a set  
                         Q 
                       of items and a complete lattice  
                         
                            ( 
                            L 
                            , 
                            ≤ 
                            ) 
                         
                       of response values, let  
                         
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                      ,  
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ∨ 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       denote the collections described as in  Notation 1 . We establish a one-to-one correspondence  
                         f 
                       between  
                         
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ∨ 
                            
                         
                      . Moreover, we demonstrate that  
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ∨ 
                            
                         
                       in the correspondence  
                         f 
                       cannot be replaced with  
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                      . More precisely, we give the domain  
                         
                            Q 
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               a 
                               , 
                               b 
                               , 
                               c 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       and the complete lattice  
                         
                            L 
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               0 
                               , 
                               t 
                               , 
                               1 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       with  
                         
                            0 
                            < 
                            t 
                            < 
                            1 
                         
                       to show that there is not any one-to-one correspondence between  
                         
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       (with respect to the given  
                         Q 
                       and  
                         L 
                      ). These results give a correction of Theorem 11 in  Stefanutti et al. (2020) . In addition, as an application of the correspondence  
                         f 
                      , we show that the pair  
                         
                            ( 
                            f 
                            , 
                            
                               
                                  f 
                               
                               
                                  − 
                                  1 
                               
                            
                            ) 
                         
                       of mappings forms a Galois connection between  
                         
                            ( 
                            
                               
                                  K 
                               
                               
                                  ⊔ 
                               
                            
                            , 
                            ⊆ 
                            ) 
                         
                       and  
                         
                            ( 
                            
                               
                                  M 
                               
                               
                                  ∨ 
                               
                            
                            , 
                            ≼ 
                            ) 
                         
                      , where  
                         ⊆ 
                       is the set inclusion relation and  
                         ≼ 
                       is the quasi order described as in  Notation 2 . Furthermore, the two sets of closed elements of this Galois connection are  
                         
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ∨ 
                            
                         
                      , respectively.

In the end, we turn our attention to an interesting question. In the dichotomous theory of knowledge structures,  Doignon and Falmagne (1999)  proved that there is a one-to-one correspondence between the collection of all granular spaces on the domain  
                         Q 
                       and the collection of all surmise functions on  
                         Q 
                      . This means that, in the polytomous theory of knowledge structures, the condition  
                         
                            L 
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               0 
                               , 
                               1 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       is sufficient to ensure that there is a one-to-one correspondence between  
                         
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                      . However, what is the necessary and sufficient condition ensuring that there is a one-to-one correspondence between  
                         
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            
                               M 
                            
                            
                               ⊔ 
                            
                         
                      ? This question is still open.
